قياس الوكالة العامة على الوكالة الخاصة
Analogy from specific agency to general agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qiyas from specific agency to general agency to identify when generality removes harmful ignorance in agency contracts.

Core Idea
Generality in agency removes harmful ignorance, making the unknown known.

In this passage, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa explains how Hanafi jurists analogize general agency from specific agency. The key legal insight is that when the scope of agency is defined as 'general', it eliminates the uncertainty that would otherwise invalidate the contract. This lesson unpacks the qiyas structure and shows how muftis apply this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original case (asl)
What is the specific agency (wakalah khassah) and what is its ruling? The passage states texts permit it.
2
Identify the new case (far')
General agency (wakalah ammah) where tasks are not individually specified.
3
Determine the effective cause (illah)
What commonality connects them? The passage says generality makes the unknown known and prevents dispute.
This is the key: in both cases, the agent's authority is known — specifically or generally.
4
Derive the ruling for the new case
Apply the permissibility from the asl to the far', then contrast with the invalid 'some of my affairs' case.
The illah of preventing harmful ignorance is present only when the scope is definitively general.
5
Apply as a mufti
When issuing a fatwa, if a client presents an agency contract with general terms, rule it valid. If the terms are vague ('some affairs'), rule it invalid by consensus.
This qiyas is a tool for fatwa construction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤ - ورد في الشريعة نصوص تجيز الوكالة الخاصة بشأن مخصوص وتثبت لها أحكاماً معينة معروفة . فقاس فقهاء الحنفية عليها الوكالة العامة في الجواز والأحكام ولم يروا بأساً بعدم تعيين الأعمال الموكل بها وجهالتها عند العقد في هذه الوكالة العامة، لأنَّ العموم يجعل المجهول كالمعلوم ويحسم النزاع بخلاف الوكالة الخاصة إذا جهل موضوعها، كمن قال الآخر : وكلتك في بعض أعمالي فإنها غير جائزة باتفاق الفقهاء.
4. Texts in Shari'ah permit specific agency concerning a specific matter and establish for it certain known rulings. The Hanafi jurists analogized general agency to it in permissibility and rulings, and they saw no harm in not specifying the delegated actions and their ignorance at the time of contract in this general agency, because generality makes the unknown like the known and prevents dispute, unlike specific agency if its subject is unknown, such as someone saying to another: 'I appoint you as my agent in some of my affairs' – this is not permissible by agreement of the jurists.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi qiyas (analogical reasoning) from specific agency (al-wakalah al-khassah) to general agency (al-wakalah al-ammah). The Hanafi jurists base their ruling on existing texts that permit specific agency; they extend that permission to general agency because the generality of the agency eliminates the uncertainty that would otherwise invalidate the contract. The key point is that in general agency, the scope of authority is broad but known as 'general', so there is no harmful ignorance. In contrast, if someone delegates 'some of my affairs' without specification, it is invalid by consensus because the subject matter is unknown. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of extending rulings through effective cause (illah): the removal of dispute through generality.

Key Terms
وكالة خاصة (wakalah khassah): Agency appointed for a specific, known task.
وكالة عامة (wakalah ammah): Agency without specifying individual tasks, covering all affairs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analogy, why is general agency valid despite the lack of specific tasks?
A) Because it is based on a clear text from the Quran
B) Because generality makes the unknown like the known and prevents dispute
C) Because the agent can refuse any task
D) Because it is a form of partnership

Key Takeaway
General agency is valid because generality removes harmful ignorance, analogized from specific agency by qiyas.

The Qiyas of Subsequent Ratification to Prior Agency
Analogy from agency to ratification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that subsequent ratification (ijazah) is equivalent to prior agency (tawkil) to cases of unauthorized acts (fuduli) and construct the qiyas argument.

Core Idea
Subsequent ratification retroactively validates a fuduli's act as if originally authorized.

This passage illustrates the Hanafi method of qiyas (analogical reasoning) by drawing an equivalence between two legal acts: prior agency and subsequent ratification. Understanding this analogy is crucial for muftis when assessing contracts entered into without direct authorization. The principle that 'ratification is like agency' underpins many rulings in mu'amalat, such as sales, marriages, and transfers of property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The case under consideration is the ratification (ijazah) by a person of an act performed on his behalf by a fuduli (unauthorized person).
2
Locate the analogical base (asl)
The base is the contract of agency (tawkil), where the principal explicitly authorizes the agent to act.
3
Determine the effective cause ('illa)
The common 'illa is the consent and authority (idaan/rida) of the principal or ratifier, which validates the agent's/fuduli's act.
The 'illa is jaliyyah (clear) because both situations involve authorization.
4
Apply the ruling
Just as a prior agency makes the agent's act effective from the start, ratification makes the fuduli's act effective as if it were authorized originally.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah)
The property or right transferred by the fuduli becomes validly transferred from the moment of the act, not from the moment of ratification.
This retroactive effect is key in determining ownership and liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٥ - وكذلك قاسوا أيضاً على عقد التوكيل إجازة الإنسان تصرفاً في بعض حقوقه صَدَر من آخر فضولاً عنه دون سابق توكيل منه، فقرروا أنَّ الإجازة اللاحقة تعتبر كالوكالة السابقة؛ فيصبح بهذه الإجازة تصرف الفضولي (١) نافذاً على المجيز كعمل الوكيل بمقتضى وكالة سابقة .
5. Similarly, they analogized to the contract of agency the ratification by a person of an act in some of his rights that originated from another as a fuduli (unauthorized agent) without prior agency from him. They ruled that subsequent ratification is considered like prior agency; thus, by this ratification, the act of the fuduli becomes effective on the ratifier like the work of an agent according to prior agency.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage shows the Hanafi qiyas from the contract of agency (tawkil) to the ratification (ijazah) of an unauthorized person's act (fuduli). The jurists hold that ratification retroactively creates the same effect as prior appointment. The analogical reasoning is that both produce the same legal consequence: the principal's (or ratifier's) consent validates the act. This is a fundamental principle in Hanafi mu'amalat: subsequent consent treats the act as if it were originally authorized.

Key Terms
فضولي (fuduli): A person who acts on behalf of another without prior authorization.
إجازة (ijazah): Subsequent permission or ratification of an act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does the Hanafi school treat subsequent ratification (ijazah) of a fuduli's act?
A) As a new independent contract requiring fresh offer and acceptance.
B) As equivalent to prior agency, making the act effective from the beginning.
C) As invalid if the fuduli was not appointed in writing.
D) As requiring a court order to be effective.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, subsequent ratification (ijazah) is legally equivalent to prior agency (tawkil) through clear analogy, giving retroactive validity to a fuduli's act.

Qiyas from Employee to Paid Agent: Binding Effect of Fee
Analogy from employee to paid agent, binding effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qiyas that transforms a non-binding agency into a binding contract when the agent takes a fee, and identify the common illa (compensation).

Core Idea
A fee turns a non-binding agent into a bound employee — compensation is the catalyst.

This passage demonstrates a classic Hanafi qiyas: the jurists analogized a paid agent (wakil bi al-ujrah) to a hired employee (ajir). Although agency is inherently non-binding, taking a fee creates a binding obligation. This shows how qiyas can modify contractual natures based on a shared effective cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Recognize that an employee (ajir) is compelled to perform the work he was hired for. This is the established ruling (asl).
The ruling is that the ajir khas is bound (mujbar).
2
Identify the new case
Consider the paid agent (wakil bi al-ujrah). Agency is originally non-binding, but the agent has taken a fee.
The far' is the paid agent.
3
Find the common illa
Identify the effective cause (illa) that both cases share: both the employee and the paid agent receive compensation for their work.
The illa is receiving compensation (ujrah).
4
Apply qiyas
Since the illa is present in the paid agent, the same ruling (compulsion to perform) applies to him.
This is qiyas jali (clear analogy).
5
Recognize the legal effect
Understand that the paid agent's contract becomes binding (lazim), unlike a gratuitous agent who can withdraw.
The fee changes the contractual nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٦ - ثبت في أحكام الشريعة أنَّ الأجير مُجْبَرٌ على القيام بما استُؤْجِرَ عليه فقاس الفقهاء عليه حكم الوكيل بالأجرة، فاعتبروه مُخبراً على القيام بما وكل به، لأنه بتقاضيه الأجر أصبح كالأجير، وإن كانت الوكالة في الأصل عقداً غير لازم أي لا يوجب إلزام الوكيل بالعمل .
6. It is established in the rulings of Shari'ah that an employee (ajir) is compelled to perform what he was hired for. The jurists analogized to him the ruling of an agent with a fee; they considered him compelled to perform what he was delegated, because by taking the fee he becomes like an employee, even though agency is originally a non-binding contract that does not obligate the agent to work.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage illustrates qiyas from the hired employee (ajir) to the paid agent (wakil bi al-ujrah). In Hanafi fiqh, the basic contract of agency is non-binding (ghayr lazim), meaning the agent can withdraw. However, when the agent takes a fee, he becomes like a hireling (ajir khas), and thus the contract becomes binding on him. The analogy is based on the common feature: both receive compensation for their work. This is a good example of how qiyas can transform the legal nature of a contract.

Key Terms
أجير (ajir): A hired person who is bound to perform the work.
وكيل بالأجرة (wakil bi al-ujrah): An agent who receives a fee for his agency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a paid agent become compelled to perform according to Hanafi qiyas?
A) Because agency is always binding
B) Because he is analogous to an employee who is compelled
C) Because the principal can force him
D) Because the contract is written

Key Takeaway
A paid agent is bound to perform because the fee makes him analogous to a hired employee in Hanafi qiyas.

Change of Name in Usurped Goods: Qiyas on Destruction
Analogy from destruction to change of name in usurpation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qiyas that a substantial change (taghyir) in a usurped item transfers the owner's right to compensation, akin to destruction.

Core Idea
Transforming a usurped item into something new terminates the owner's right to the original and replaces it with compensation.

This passage examines a key Hanafi principle: when a usurper alters the usurped property so fundamentally that its name changes (e.g., steel into sword, wheat into flour), it is treated as destruction. The owner's right transfers from the specific object to a guarantee of its like or value. This qiyas jali (clear analogy) is based on the hadith 'on the hand what it took until it returns it'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Base Ruling
The established ruling (asl) is that if a usurped item perishes, the usurper must compensate the owner with its like or value, and the owner's right transfers to this guarantee.
This is based on the hadith and ijma'.
2
Identify the New Case
The new case (far') is where the usurper changes the item so its name/essence changes (e.g., steel→sword, wheat→flour). The item still exists physically but in a transformed state.
The transformation is not mere use but a change in identity.
3
Determine the Illa (Effective Cause)
The common illa is the loss of the specific original item in a form that can be returned. In both cases, the original is no longer returnable as such.
The Hanafis consider name change as indicative of substantive change.
4
Apply the Qiyas and State the Ruling
Applying qiyas: just as destruction ends the owner's right to the specific item and triggers compensation, so too does a change of name. The owner can demand the value, not the transformed item.
This is the Hanafi position used in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۷ - ثبت بنصوص الشريعة أنَّ مَنْ غَصَبَ شيئاً وَجَب عليه رد عينه ما عنده، فإنْ تَلِفَ المغصوب يضمن الغاصب للمالك مثله أو قيمته، وينتقل حق المالك إلى هذا التضمين عوضاً عن الأصل الهالك؛ وذلك بقوله : على اليد ما أخذت حتى تؤديه»(۲). فقاس فقهاء الحنفية على هلاك المغصوب ما لو أحدث فيه الغاصب له به اسم جديد، كما لو غَصَب قطعة فولاذ فصنعها سيفاً، تغييراً يحدث أو طحن الحنطة المغصوبة حتى صارت دقيقاً، فاعتبروا هذا التغيير كالاستهلاك، إذ قد تغير به الاسم فأصبح شيئاً آخر ؛ فقالوا: إن حق المالك حينئذ ينقطع من عين المغصوب وينتقل حقه إلى تضمين الغاصب، كحكم الإتلاف المقيس عليه .
7. It is established by texts of Shari'ah that whoever usurps something must return the specific item if it is still in his possession, but if the usurped item perishes, the usurper guarantees to the owner its like or value, and the owner's right transfers to this guarantee as a substitute for the perished original; that is by His saying (SAW): 'The hand must return what it took until it gives it back.' The Hanafi jurists analogized to the perishing of the usurped item the case where the usurper brings about a new name/essence in it, such as if he usurps a piece of steel and makes it into a sword, a change that creates a new name, or grinds usurped wheat until it becomes flour; they considered this change like consumption, because the name changed and it became something else. They said: The owner's right then ceases from the specific usurped item and transfers to the guarantee of the usurper, like the ruling of destruction upon which it is analogized.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents a qiyas from the destruction (halak) of a usurped item to a substantial change (taghyir) that changes its name/essence. The Hanafi jurists reason that just as perishing obligates the guarantor to pay compensation ending the owner's claim to the original, similarly, a transformation like making steel into a sword or grinding wheat into flour results in a new item, so the owner's right is replaced by a monetary compensation. The proof is the hadith 'on the hand what it took until it returns it,' which implies return of the specific object unless it is no longer possible. This principle is important in Hanafi fiqh for cases of misappropriation and transformation.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation of someone's property without right.
تضمين (tadmin): Liability to pay compensation (like or value).
تغيير الاسم (taghyir al-ism): Change of name/essence that renders the item legally different.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning from an established ruling to a new case sharing the same effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi qiyas, what happens to the owner's right if the usurper grinds wheat into flour?
A) The owner can take the flour
B) The owner's right transfers to compensation (like or value)
C) The owner must wait for the flour to become bread
D) The owner has no right to anything

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: if a usurped item is transformed so it changes its name, the owner's right becomes a claim for compensation, not the altered item.

The Qiyas of Silence: From Permission to Ratification
Analogy from silence at permission to silence after contract for marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the qiyas between silence at permission and silence after a fuduli marriage contract, and apply the Hanafi principle of customary indication (dalalah urfiyyah) to analogous cases in fatwa.

Core Idea
A virgin's silence is consent by custom – the same logic extends to her silence after a fuduli marriage contract.

This passage introduces a classic Hanafi analogy (qiyas) rooted in a sahih hadith. The Prophet (SAW) ruled that a virgin's silence when asked for marriage consent counts as consent due to customary shyness. Hanafi jurists extended this reasoning: if a guardian contracts her marriage without prior permission (fuduli), her subsequent silence upon hearing the news is also considered ratification (ijazah) by the same customary indication. This shows how qiyas operates alongside 'urf to cover new scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling (asl)
The hadith states that a virgin's silence when asked for permission for marriage constitutes consent. This is the established ruling (hukm) for the case of prior permission.
The hadith is authentic; 'صماتها' means her silence is her consent.
2
Identify the new case (far')
The new case is where the guardian contracts the marriage without seeking permission first (fuduli), and then the woman remains silent after being informed.
This scenario is not directly addressed by the hadith but is analogous.
3
Determine the common effective cause (illah)
The illah is the customary indication (dalalah urfiyyah) that a virgin's silence in marriage matters indicates consent due to shyness. This illah is present in both the original and new cases.
Shyness (haya') is a recognized custom ('urf) that gives meaning to silence.
4
Apply the qiyas
Since the illah is the same, the ruling of consent is transferred from the original to the new case. Her silence after the contract is legally treated as ratification (ijazah).
This qiyas is considered jaliy (clear) because the illah is explicit and shared.
5
Confirm with the governing qawida
The underlying legal maxim: 'الأمور بمقاصدها' and specifically 'العادة محكمة' (custom is authoritative). Customary indication is a valid basis for legal rulings in the Hanafi school.
This ties to the broader principle of istihsan and 'urf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۸ - ورد في الحديث النبوي بشأن التوكيل في عقد النكاح أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال عن الفتاة البكر البالغة: «إذنها صُماتها» (١) . أي إنها إذا استأذنها وليها بعقد نكاحها فسكتت يعتبر سكوتها توكيلاً، بمقتضى الدلالة العرفية، لأنها يغلب عليها في هذا المقام الخجل عادة. فقاس الفقهاء عليه ما لو زوجها وليها فضولاً دون استثمارها - أي استئذانها - ثم بلغها الخبر فسكتت فاعتبر الفقهاء سكوتها بعد العقد إجازة منها دلالة عرفية، كما اعتُبِرَ سكوتها عند استثمارها إذناً منها.
8. It is reported in the prophetic hadith concerning agency in the marriage contract that the Prophet (SAW) said about the mature virgin girl: 'Her consent is her silence.' That is, if her guardian asks her permission for her marriage and she remains silent, her silence is considered permission (agency) by customary indication, because shyness usually overcomes her in this situation. The jurists analogized to it the case where her guardian marries her off as a fuduli without consulting her (i.e., without seeking her permission), then the news reaches her and she remains silent; the jurists considered her silence after the contract as ratification by customary indication, just as her silence at the time of seeking permission was considered consent.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage presents a qiyas from the established ruling that a virgin's silence when asked for permission for marriage counts as consent (based on the hadith), to the case where a guardian acts without prior permission but the woman remains silent upon hearing the news. The Hanafi jurists extend the principle of customary indication (al-dalalah al-urfiyyah) to treat her subsequent silence as ratification (ijazah) of the contract. This shows how qiyas is used to cover situations not explicitly mentioned in the text, based on common practice and custom.

Key Terms
صمات (sumat): Silence (of a virgin) which is considered consent.
دلالة عرفية (dalalah urfiyyah): Customary indication; a meaning understood by custom rather than explicit words.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the analogy, what does a virgin's silence after being informed of her marriage signify?
A) Dissent
B) Ratification by customary indication
C) A need to consult again
D) Invalid contract

Key Takeaway
Customary indication (dalalah urfiyyah) allows silence to signify consent in specific contexts, and this principle extends by qiyas to similar cases.

Qiyas and the Basis of Khiyar al-Shart
Analogy from the hadith of the deceived buyer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the hadith basis for khiyar al-shart and apply qiyas to extend the ruling to general sales contracts.

Core Idea
The Prophet's permission for a deceived buyer to stipulate a three-day option is the basis for the general permissibility of khiyar al-shart.

This lesson examines how a specific Prophetic guidance given to a companion who was frequently cheated in sales became the foundation for a major principle in Hanafi contract law: the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart). You will see how the Hanafi school uses qiyas to extend this specific permission to all sales where a party needs time to deliberate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original case (asl)
Identify the specific scenario the hadith addresses: a companion (Ibn Munqidh) complained of being cheated; the Prophet allowed him to stipulate a three-day option.
The asl is the hadith itself: a specific buyer granted an option due to deception.
2
Extract the effective cause (illa)
Determine the illa: the buyer's need for deliberation to avoid being cheated (ghabn). This is the reason the option was allowed.
The Prophet's words 'no cheating' indicate the illa is prevention of deception.
3
Identify the new case (far)
The far is any buyer (or seller) who fears being cheated and stipulates a similar option in a sales contract.
The far is not limited to frequent cheaters; it covers all who need time to deliberate.
4
Apply qiyas to derive the ruling
Since the illa (need to avoid deception) is present in the far, the same ruling applies: stipulating an option is permissible, and the option period may be up to three days.
Qiyas jaliy: clear analogy because the illa is explicitly indicated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۹ - ثبت في السنة تجويز اشتراط الخيار للمشتري في عقد البيع، أي اشتراط حق الفسخ أو الإبرام خلال مدة معينة ويسمى: خيار الشرط، لأنَّ المشتري قد يحتاج إلى التروي خشية الغبن فقد شكا أحد الصحابة، وهو بن منقذ، إلى النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه كثيراً ما يغبن في البيوع، فأرشده إلى اشتراط الخيار بقوله : إذا بايعت فقل : لاخلابة(٢)، ولي الخيار ثلاثة أيام (۳).
9. It is established in the Sunnah to permit stipulating a choice (option) for the buyer in a sales contract, i.e., stipulating the right of cancellation or confirmation within a specified period, and it is called khiyar al-shart, because the buyer may need to deliberate for fear of being cheated. One of the companions, Ibn Munqidh (or Habbān ibn Munqidh), complained to the Prophet (SAW) that he was often cheated in sales, so he guided him to stipulate an option, saying: 'When you buy, say: No cheating, and I have an option for three days.'
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is not an explicit qiyas but rather narrates the basis for khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) directly from a hadith. It shows that the Hanafi ruling permitting stipulating an option in sales originates from a specific Sunnah where the Prophet allowed a companion who was frequently cheated to stipulate a three-day option. The jurists then analogized from this specific case to the general permissibility of khiyar al-shart in any sale where the buyer needs deliberation. The passage illustrates how a specific ruling can be extended through qiyas to other similar cases.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in a contract allowing either party to cancel or confirm within a set period.
خلابة (khalabah): Cheating or deception in a transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis in the Sunnah for khiyar al-shart?
A) A Quranic verse
B) The Prophet's guidance to a complaining companion to stipulate a three-day option
C) General consensus
D) The practice of the Caliphs

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart is rooted in a specific hadith and extended by qiyas to all sales where a party needs deliberation, subject to the three-day guideline.

6 min
Rule: One is Bound by His Own Acknowledgment
Expansion of a Hanafi maxim with furuat on debt and deposit agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-mar'u mu'akhadh bi-iqrarihi' to distinguish between cases where acknowledgment binds the person and where it does not, and state the mufta bihi ruling for the deposit case.

Core Idea
Your acknowledgment binds you only; it cannot bind others or affect their property.

This lesson unpacks a central Hanafi maxim regarding the binding force of acknowledgments. The maxim states that a person is held accountable for his own acknowledgment, but not for acknowledging on behalf of another. We will explore its application through two contrasting scenarios: debt and deposit. Understanding this distinction is crucial for issuing fatwa in agency and property disputes.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its core meaning
Read the Arabic maxim: 'المرء مؤاخذ بإقراره في حق نفسه لا في حق غيره'. Understand that it establishes a personal liability; one's acknowledgment affects only his own rights and obligations.
The maxim is a dabt (sub-maxim) that restricts the general rule of iqrar.
2
Identify the first furu': debt agency
Consider the case where a debtor acknowledges that a claimant is the agent of his creditor. According to the maxim, this acknowledgment binds the debtor personally. So he must pay the claimant the debt, because he is paying from his own wealth.
The payment is from the debtor's own property; his acknowledgment is against himself.
3
Identify the second furu': deposit agency
Now consider the case where a depositary acknowledges that a claimant is the agent of the depositor. Here, the maxim does NOT compel the depositary to hand over the deposit. Why? Because the deposit is the property of another; the acknowledgment would affect the owner's right, not the depositary's own right.
This is a clear istithna' (exception) to a surface application of the maxim.
4
Understand the underlying reason (istihsan vs qiyas)
At first glance, qiyas (analogy) with the debt case would suggest the depositary must hand over. However, the Hanafi school prefers istihsan because the owner's right is attached to the specific property (ayn), while in debt it is attached to the liability (dhimma). Handing over the deposit without proof risks loss to the owner.
The istihsan overrides qiyas to protect ownership rights.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its implications
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the istihsan ruling: the depositary is not obliged to hand over the deposit based solely on his own acknowledgment. The claimant must bring proof from the owner. This ruling is found in the later authoritative works like al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
In fatwa, always verify whether the acknowledgment affects only the acknowledging person or involves another's right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢ - من القواعد المقررة أنَّ المرء مؤاخذ بإقراره في حق نفسه لا في حق غيره فلو أقرَّ مثلاً أنه وأخاه مدينان بمبلغ يلزم هو بما يصيبه منه، ولا يلزم أخوه إن أنكر وعلى هذا لو ادعى شخص أنه وكيل عن دائن غائب بقبض دَيْنه، فأقر المدين بوكالته يؤمر بدفع الدين إليه عملاً بإقراره. وبناء عليه، إذا أودع أحد شيئاً عند آخر وغاب. فادَّعى شخص أنه وكيل الغائب في قبض وديعته، فأقر الوديع له بالوكالة، فإن مقتضى القياس الظاهر على مسألة قبض الدين أن يُلزم الوديع بتسليم الوديعة إليه. لكن الاستحسان عدم إلزام الوديع بتسليم الوديعة إليه ولو كان الوديع بوكالته لاحتمال أن يحضر صاحب الوديعة فينكر التوكيل، وتكون وديعته قد ذهبت وربما لا يمكن استردادها، وإن حقه متعلق بعينها. بخلاف صورة الدين، فإنَّ حق الدائن فيها متعلّق بذمة المدين لا بعين المبلغ الذي يدفعه هذا المدين إلى زاعم الوكالة بالقبض. فإذا حَضَر الدائن فأنكر الوكالة يتبين أن الدفع السابق لم يكن قضاء صحيحاً للدين، لعدم ثبوت وكالة القابض، فيكون حق الدائن باقياً على حاله في ذمة المدين، ويكلف بالدفع ثانية إلى الدائن، وله حق الرجوع على القابض ليسترد منه ما دفعه إليه، فيؤمر بالدفع ثانية إلى الألف الذي أنكر الوكالة. وإيضاح ذلك أن عملية وفاء الدين في الواقع وبالنظر الفقهي هي أنَّ المدين يدفع من مال نفسه ما يعادل الدين فإقراره بوكالة القبض هو اعتراف منه بلزوم تسليم ماله إلى مدَّعي الوكالة وفاء لدين الدائن، فهو إقرار على نفسه، فإذا لم تثبت الوكالة فيما بعد كان هو المفرط في مال نفسه فيؤمر بالدفع ثانية إلى الدائن الذي أنكر الوكالة.
أما الوديعة فإنَّ حق مالكها متعلق بعينها ذاتها لا بذمة الوديع. فيكون إقرار الوديع بوكالة قبضها اعترافاً منه بلزوم تسليم مال غيره إلى شخص ثالث. فهو إقرار على غيره لا على نفسه ؛ فلو أنفذناه كان ذلك تفريطاً في حق المالك بمجرد إقرار غيره . (ر ) الدر المختار ورد المحتار، باب الوكالة بالخصومة والقبض ٤١٣/٤ - ٤١٤)
2 - Among the established rules is that a person is held accountable for his acknowledgment in his own right, not in the right of others. So if, for example, he acknowledges that he and his brother are debtors of an amount, he is bound by what falls to him, but his brother is not bound if he denies. And based on this, if a person claims that he is an agent for an absent creditor to collect his debt, and the debtor acknowledges his agency, he is ordered to pay the debt to him by virtue of his acknowledgment. Consequently, if someone deposits something with another and then is absent, and a person claims that he is the agent of the absent one to collect his deposit, and the depositary acknowledges his agency, then the requirement of apparent analogy regarding the matter of collecting a debt would be that the depositary is compelled to hand over the deposit to him. But istihsan is that the depositary is not compelled to hand over the deposit to him, even if the depositary acknowledges his agency, because of the possibility that the owner of the deposit might come and deny the agency, and his deposit would have gone, and perhaps it cannot be recovered, and his right is attached to the specific property itself. Unlike the case of a debt, for the creditor's right therein is attached to the debtor's liability, not to the specific sum that this debtor pays to the claimant of agency for collection. So if the creditor comes and denies the agency, it becomes clear that the previous payment was not a valid discharge of the debt, due to the lack of proof of the agent's agency; thus the creditor's right remains as it was in the debtor's liability, and he (the debtor) is made to pay again to the creditor, and he has the right to recourse against the claimant to recover what he paid him. He is ordered to pay a second time to the one who denied the agency. Clarifying this: the process of discharging a debt, in reality and in juristic view, is that the debtor pays from his own wealth an amount equivalent to the debt; so his acknowledgment of the agency for collection is an admission from him of the obligation to hand over his money to the claimant of agency as a discharge of the creditor's debt. Thus it is an acknowledgment against himself. So if the agency is not later proven, it is he who was negligent with his own wealth, and he is ordered to pay again to the creditor who denied the agency. As for the deposit, the owner's right is attached to the specific property itself, not to the depositary's liability. Thus the depositary's acknowledgment of agency for its collection is an admission from him of the obligation to hand over someone else's property to a third party. It is an acknowledgment against others, not against himself. So if we were to enforce it, that would be negligence towards the owner's right merely by someone else's acknowledgment. (See al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Radd al-Muhtar, chapter of agency for litigation and collection, 4/413-414).
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage presents a well-established Hanafi qawida (legal maxim): one is held accountable for his own acknowledgment, not for the acknowledgment of others. It then applies this maxim to two contrasting cases: debt and deposit. In the case of debt, if a debtor acknowledges that someone is the agent of his creditor, he must pay the debt to that agent because the payment is from his own wealth; his acknowledgment binds himself. In the case of a deposit (wadi'a), if the depositary acknowledges someone as the agent of the absent owner, he is not compelled to hand over the deposit, because the owner's right is attached to the specific property. Handing it over based on the depositary's own acknowledgment would affect the owner's property, which is an acknowledgment against another. This difference is based on istihsan, which overrides qiyas in the deposit case to protect the owner's property. The authority weight is from later Hanafi works (Fatawa/Mutakhkhirin), specifically al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Radd al-Muhtar.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrar): اعتراف الشخص بحق عليه أو بوكالة غيره.
الوكالة بالقبض (al-wikala bi al-qabd): تفويض شخص آخر لاستلام ما له من دين أو وديعة.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
إذا ادعى شخص أنه وكيل عن مالك غائب في قبض وديعة، فأقر الوديع بوكالته، فهل يجب على الوديع تسليم الوديعة له حسب المذهب الحنفي؟
A) نعم، يجب تسليمها عملاً بالإقرار
B) لا يجب، بل يستحب
C) لا يجب، لأنه إقرار على الغير
D) يجب إذا كان الوديع ثقة

Key Takeaway
Your acknowledgment can only bind you and your own rights; it cannot affect the property of another without additional proof.

Istihsan in Mortgage: Qiyas vs. Istihsan after Debt Release
Demonstrates Hanafi istihsan by comparing qiyas and istihsan in mortgage liability after release.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to distinguish the qiyas ruling from the istihsan ruling in a mortgage case, and identify the illa (effective cause) that justifies the istihsan.

Core Idea
After ibra', the mortgagee is not liable because the mortgage is rescinded and the property becomes a trust.

Mortgage liability after debt discharge might seem straightforward: the mortgagee remains liable until the property is returned. However, Hanafi jurists employ istihsan to reach a different conclusion. In this lesson, you will examine a passage from Mustafa al-Zarqa's work that contrasts the apparent analogy with the preferred istihsan, revealing how the mortgagee's act of releasing the debtor implicitly rescinds the security, transforming the property into a trust. This demonstrates the operative role of istihsan in Hanafi mu'amalat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Base Rule
Start with the general principle: the mortgaged property is a security (daman) against the mortgagee to the extent of the debt. If the property perishes in his hands while equal to the debt, he is liable. This is the foundation for the analogy.
2
Distinguish the Two Scenarios
The text compares two scenarios: (1) the debt is collected (istifa') and then property perishes; (2) the debt is released (ibra') and then property perishes. The qiyas treats them similarly because in both cases the property is still in the mortgagee's hands.
3
Trace the Qiyas Argument
The apparent qiyas argues: just as after collection the mortgagee remains liable until return, so after release he also remains liable. The illa (effective cause) is the continued existence of the security interest until physical return.
This is the strict analogy (qiyas jali).
4
Understand the Istihsan Objection
Istihsan holds that release (ibra') is not analogous to collection. By releasing, the mortgagee voluntarily gives up his right to the debt, which effectively rescinds the mortgage contract (faskh al-rahn). Thus the property becomes an amana (trust) in his hands.
The mortgagee has the independent right to rescind; consequently, liability arises only from wrongful conduct.
5
Apply the Mufta Bihi Ruling
The relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi) is the istihsan position: after ibra', the mortgagee is not liable for accidental destruction. This is supported by later authorities like Radd al-Muhtar.
This shows how istihsan overrides qiyas when a stronger consideration exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣ - من المقرَّر فقهاً أنَّ المرهون مضمون على الدائن المرتهن بما يعادل الدين، فإذا هَلَكَ المرهون في يده، وكانت قيمته مساوية للذين [؟] سقط إنَّ المرتهن لو كان قد استوفى الدين قبل هلاك المرهون يرد الدين. حتى ما استوفاه. وعلى هذا لو أبرأ الدائن المرتهن ذمَّة المدين عن دينه، ثم هلك المرهون قبل إعادته، فإنَّ مقتضى القياس الظاهر أن يضمن المرتهن للراهن قيمته قياساً لحالة الإبراء على حالة الاستيفاء، إذ يبقى المرهون مضموناً بعد استيفاء الدين حتى يعاد. ولكن الاستحسان عدم ضمان المرهون بعد الإبراء عن الدين، واعتبار المرتهن بعد إبرائه للمدين كالفاسخ للرهن لأن الدائن المرتهن يستقل بفسخ الرهن، إذ هو توثيق لحقه، وإذا فسخه انقلب المرهون أمانة في يده، فلا يضمن هلاكه عندئذ إلا بالتعدي عليه أو التقصير في حفظه (ر: رد المحتار ٣٣٥/٥ و ٣٣٨) .
3. It is established in fiqh that the mortgaged property is a security (daman) against the creditor-mortgagee to the extent of the debt. So if the mortgaged property perishes in his hand while its value equals the debt, [if] the mortgagee had already collected the debt before the destruction, he returns the debt — even what he collected. And on this basis, if the creditor-mortgagee releases the debtor's liability (dhimma) from the debt, then the mortgaged property perishes before its return, the requirement of apparent qiyas (analogy) is that the mortgagee is liable to the mortgagor for its value, by analogy from the case of collection (istifa') to the case of release (ibra'), since the mortgaged property remains a security after the collection of debt until it is returned. However, istihsan (juristic preference) holds that the mortgaged property is not guaranteed after the release from the debt, and considers the mortgagee after his release of the debtor to be like one who rescinds the mortgage (faskh al-rahn). Because the creditor-mortgagee has the independent right to rescind the mortgage, since it is a security for his right. If he rescinds it, the mortgaged property becomes an amana (trust) in his hand, so he is not liable for its destruction unless through transgression (ta'addi) or negligence (taqsir) in its preservation. (Reference: Radd al-Muhtar 5/335 and 338).
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage discusses a Hanafi ruling on the liability of the mortgagee (murtahin) after the debt is discharged. Normally, the mortgaged property is held as security (daman) against the mortgagee; if it is destroyed in his possession while equal to the debt, he is liable to the mortgagor (rahin) for its value because he already benefited from the debt. The apparent qiyas (analogy) extends this liability to the case where the debt is released (ibra') before the property is returned: since the property remains as security until returned, the mortgagee should be liable if it perishes after release but before return. However, the Hanafi school applies istihsan here: the mortgagee is not liable after ibra'. The reasoning is that by releasing the debt, the mortgagee effectively rescinds the mortgage contract (faskh al-rahn). As the mortgage is a security only for his right, he has the authority to terminate it. Once rescinded, the mortgaged property becomes a mere trust (amana) in his hands, like a deposit. Consequently, he is only liable if he causes loss through transgression or negligence, not if it perishes naturally. This istihsan overrides the strict analogy to avoid hardship and to align with the nature of the mortgage as a consensual security.

Key Terms
الرهن (al-rahn): A contract of mortgage where property is held as security for a debt.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that deviates from strict qiyas due to a stronger consideration.
الإبراء (al-ibra'): Release or discharge from a debt, extinguishing the obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi istihsan in this passage, when does the mortgagee cease to be liable for the mortgaged property?
A) Immediately upon the debt being released (ibra').
B) Only when the property is physically returned.
C) Never, the mortgagee is always liable.
D) Only when the mortgagee is negligent.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, istihsan can override qiyas when the mortgagee's release of the debt is treated as a rescission of the security, making the property a trust and eliminating liability for accidental loss.

Istihsan al-Darura: Definition and Application in Employee Liability
Defines istihsan of necessity and applies it to employee liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define istihsan al-darura and apply it to distinguish between the liability of specific and general employees in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Istihsan al-darura deviates from qiyas to avoid hardship; general employees are liable for loss even without negligence.

This passage defines istihsan al-darura, a key Hanafi usul tool that allows deviation from qiyas when strict analogy leads to hardship. It then demonstrates the concept through a classic example: the liability of employees. Under qiyas, all employees are trustees and not liable for loss. But by istihsan, the Hanafis distinguish between the specific employee (ajir khas) and the general employee (ajir mushtarak), holding the latter liable. This lesson unpacks the definition, the reasoning, and the practical ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Locate the definition of istihsan al-darura in the text: it is a deviation from qiyas due to necessity or public interest to remove hardship.
The source defines it as 'that which is opposed to the ruling of qiyas due to a compelling necessity or an exigent interest'.
2
Understand the rationale
Notice why qiyas is set aside: applying qiyas consistently would lead to hardship (haraj) in some cases, so a different ruling is adopted to achieve ease and justice.
The text explains that analogous cases may differ in their circumstances, so strict analogy can yield unjust results.
3
Recall the general rule of trustees
The text states the established shar'i rule: a trustee (amin) is not liable for loss unless he transgresses or is negligent. This is the default qiyas for all trustees.
Examples given: depositary, partner, lessee, borrower.
4
See the extension by qiyas to employees
By qiyas, an employee (ajir) should also be treated as a trustee and not liable. But the Hanafis deviate by istihsan.
The text says 'accordingly, he should not be liable at all.'
5
Learn the istihsan distinction
The Hanafis distinguish between the specific employee (ajir khas) and the general employee (ajir mushtarak). The specific employee is a trustee; the general employee is liable by istihsan.
General employee works for multiple clients, so he is like a bailee for hire and is liable even without negligence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الثاني: استحسان الضرورة ٥/٤ - وأما استحسان الضرورة فهو ما خولف فيه حكم القياس نظراً إلى ضرورة موجبة أو مصلحة مقتضية سداً للحاجة أو دفعاً للخرج. الفصل (٤) المصادر التبعية الاستحسان فمحله عندما يكون اطراد الحكم القياسي مؤدياً لحرج أو مشكلة في بعض المسائل؛ فيعدل حينئذ عنه استحساناً إلى حكم آخر يزول به الحرج وتندفع به المشكلة وذلك لأن المسائل التي يقاس بعضها على بعض - وإن كانت من جنس واحد وقائمة على أسس مشتركة - قد تختلف نتائجها عدلاً وجوراً، أو عسراً ويسراً باختلاف موضوعاتها وما يكتنفها من عوارض وملابسات. فالاستحسان يكون في مثل هذا طريقاً للفقهاء إلى الأحكام المصلحية التي تتفق مع المنطق الفقهي ومقاصد الشريعة عندما يلوح في اطراد القياس سوء النتائج. وهذا النوع من الاستحسان يرجع في الحقيقة إلى نظرية المصالح المرسلة الآتي بيانها في البحث التالي، كما سنرى. ٦/٤ - أمثلة استحسان الضرورة ومن أمثلة استحسان الضرورة المسائل التالية : من المقرر شرعاً أن الأمين كالوديع مثلاً، إذا هلك لديه مال الأمانة بلا تعد ولا تقصير في حفظه لا يضمن شيئاً من قيمته. ويستمر القياس كذلك في كل أمانة بيد أمين، كمال الشركة في يد أحد الشريكين والمأجور في يد المستأجر والعارية في يد المستعير الخ ... ومن ذلك مال المستأجر في يد الأجير، فينبغي أن لا يضمن مطلقاً إذا تلف بلا تعدّ عليه من الأجير ولا تقصير منه في حفظه. ولكنهم فرقوا في الاستحسان بين الأجير الخاص وهو الذي يبيع وقته جميعاً لمستأجره ليعمل عنده ولا يشتغل في فراغه عند سواه، كالخادم والسائس ونحوهما، وبين الأجير العام أو المشترك وهو الذي يبيع عمله في مهنة معينة لكل راغب كالصباغ والخباز والنجار إلخ .. فقالوا : إن الأجير المشترك إذا هلك مال مستأجره لديه يضمنه استحساناً على خلاف القياس،
Second Section: Istihsan of Necessity. 5/4 - As for istihsan of necessity, it is that which is opposed to the ruling of qiyas due to a compelling necessity or an exigent interest to meet a need or repel hardship. Chapter (4) Subsidiary Sources: Istihsan. Its place is when the consistent application of the qiyasi ruling leads to hardship or a problem in some cases; then one deviates from it by istihsan to another ruling that removes the hardship and repels the problem. This is because cases that are analogized to each other—even if they are of the same type and based on common foundations—may differ in their outcomes with respect to justice/injustice or ease/difficulty depending on their subjects and surrounding circumstances. Thus istihsan becomes in such cases a way for jurists to reach maslaha-based rulings that agree with fiqh logic and the objectives of Shari'a when the consistent application of qiyas yields bad results. This type of istihsan in fact reverts to the theory of maslaha mursala (unregulated public interest) which will be explained in the following discussion, as we will see. 6/4 - Examples of Istihsan of Necessity. Among the examples of istihsan of necessity are the following issues: It is established in Shari'a that the trustee (amin), such as the depositary, if property in his custody perishes without transgression or negligence on his part in preserving it, he is not liable for any of its value. The qiyas continues likewise in every trust in the hand of a trustee, such as partnership property in the hand of one partner, rented property in the hand of the lessee, borrowed property in the hand of the borrower, etc. And from that is the property of the hirer in the hand of the employee (ajir); accordingly, he should not be liable at all if it perishes without transgression by the employee or negligence in preserving it. However, they made a distinction by istihsan between the specific employee (ajir khas), who sells all his time to his hirer to work for him and does not work for anyone else in his free time, like a servant, a groom, and the like, and the general or common employee (ajir 'am or mushtarak), who sells his work in a particular profession to anyone who wants, like a dyer, a baker, a carpenter, etc. They said: The general employee, if the property of his hirer perishes in his hand, is liable by istihsan, contrary to qiyas.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage introduces the concept of istihsan al-darura (istihsan of necessity), a key tool in Hanafi usul. It begins by defining it as a deviation from qiyas due to necessity or interest. The author explains that sometimes applying qiyas consistently leads to hardship (haraj) or problems, so scholars turn to another ruling by istihsan. This is because analogous cases may have different circumstances affecting their outcomes. This type of istihsan is connected to the theory of maslaha mursala (public interest not explicitly mentioned in texts). The passage then provides a classic example: the general rule that trustees (amana holders) are not liable for loss without negligence. By qiyas, an employee should also not be liable. However, by istihsan, the Hanafis distinguish between two types of employees: the specific employee (ajir khas) who devotes his time to one employer and is treated as a trustee, and the general employee (ajir mushtarak) who works for multiple clients. The general employee is held liable for loss of the hirer's property, even without negligence, because he is akin to a bailee for hire or because of custom and need to protect the owner's property. This ruling by istihsan overrides the apparent qiyas. The example illustrates how istihsan operates to achieve practical justice when strict analogy would cause harm.

Key Terms
استحسان الضرورة (istihsan al-darura): A type of istihsan that deviates from qiyas to avoid hardship due to necessity or public interest.
الأجير الخاص (al-ajir al-khas): A specific employee who hires out all his time to a single employer.
الأجير المشترك (al-ajir al-mushtarak): A general or common employee who works for multiple clients in a specific trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Istihsan al-darura overrides qiyas when strict analogy leads to hardship, as seen in the liability of general employees.

Istihsan al-Darurah: Two Classic Furūʿ
Two illustrative cases of istihsan al-darurah from Hanafi fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida of istihsan al-darurah to identify when a common worker is liable for loss and when a payer can reclaim payment made without prior order.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas when strict analogy causes hardship, as in common worker liability and compulsory payment.

Sometimes the strict application of qiyas (analogy) leads to outcomes that are impractical or unfair. In such cases, the Hanafi school invokes istihsan (juristic preference) to reach a ruling that better serves the public interest and avoids hardship. This lesson explores two classic furūʿ where istihsan al-darurah (juristic preference due to necessity) overrides the general rule: the liability of a common hired worker for loss of goods, and the right of a person who pays another's debt under compulsion to reclaim the amount.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule (Qiyas)
State the default rule that applies to trustees: a trustee (like a depositary) is not liable for loss without negligence. This is the qiyas that would also apply to hired workers.
This establishes the baseline: no liability without transgression or negligence.
2
Recognize the Distinction by Istihsan
Note that for the common hired worker (ajir mushtarak), the rule changes: he is liable for loss even without negligence, unless the loss is unavoidable (e.g., overwhelming fire). This is the exception (istihsan).
The private worker (ajir khas) remains under the general rule.
3
Analyze the Rationale ('Illah) for the Exception
The reason (ʿillah) for holding the common worker liable is to prevent him from over-accepting work beyond his capacity for profit, which would endanger people's property. This necessity (darurah) triggers istihsan.
The ʿillah is the risk of greed-induced negligence.
4
Examine the Second Furuʿ
The second example: a person who pays another's debt without order is normally a volunteer (mutabarriʿ) and cannot reclaim. However, if the payer is compelled (e.g., to release his own pledged property), he can reclaim. This is another application of istihsan to prevent hardship.
The compelling necessity (idṭirār) is the key factor.
5
Connect to the Qawida
Both examples illustrate the same qawida: istihsan al-darurah overrides qiyas when strict adherence to qiyas would cause undue hardship or harm. The qawida operates in muʿāmalāt to achieve practical justice.
This qawida is related to the maxim 'Harm must be removed' (al-ḍarar yuzāl).

(۲) من صور الاضطرار إلى الأداء عن الغير ما لو كان مال الإنسان مرهوناً بإذنه في دين على غيره ـ وهي مسألة المستعار للرهن - والمدين لا يفكه فإنَّ للمالك أن يفك الرهن عن ماله بأن يدفع دين المدين ويرجع عليه، ولا يعتبر متبرعاً لاضطراره إلى تخليص ماله (ر الدر المختار ورد المحتار (٣٣١/٥ .
6/4 - Examples of Istihsan al-Darurah. Among the examples of istihsan al-darurah are the following issues: It is established in Sharia that a trustee, such as a depositary, if entrusted property perishes without transgression or negligence in its preservation, he is not liable for any of its value. This analogy continues for every trust in the hands of a trustee, such as partnership property in the hand of one partner, leased property in the hand of a lessee, borrowed property in the hand of a borrower, etc. And from that is the property of a hirer in the hand of a hired worker; it would be analogically required that he is not liable at all if it perishes without transgression or negligence in its preservation. But they made a distinction by istihsan between a private hired worker (ajir khas) who sells all his time to a hirer to work for him and does not work for others during his free time, like a servant, groom, etc., and a general or common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) who sells his work in a specific profession to all who want, like a dyer, baker, carpenter, etc. They said: The common hired worker, if the property of his hirer perishes in his hand, he guarantees it by istihsan contrary to analogy, unless the destruction is due to something unavoidable like an overwhelming fire. This is so that he does not accept more work from people than his capacity out of greed for increased profit, thereby exposing their property to destruction or loss due to long storage. This ruling has been adopted by Maliki ijtihad as well for the sake of maslaha. (1) 2 - Among the established rules in Islamic fiqh is that whoever pays something from his wealth on behalf of another without his order in payment of maintenance, or settling a debt, or fulfilling any other financial right, he is considered a volunteer in what he paid on behalf of the other, whether he intended to donate or not, and he has no recourse against the one on whose behalf he paid unless the payer was compelled to pay. (2) Based on this, if someone gives money to another and orders him to buy something with it, or pay off his debt with it, or spend it on his family or building etc., and the agent keeps the money given to him, and he buys, pays, or spends from his own money for that purpose, he has no recourse... [footnote: (1) Shaikh Muhammad Abu Zahra said... (2) Examples of compulsion to pay on behalf of another include when one's property is pledged as collateral for a debt of another—this is the issue of 'musta'ar li al-rahn'—and the debtor does not redeem it, then the owner can redeem his property by paying the debtor's debt and reclaim it from him, and he is not considered a volunteer due to his compulsion to free his property.]
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage provides two classic examples of istihsan al-darurah (juristic preference due to necessity) from Hanafi fiqh. The first example concerns the liability of a common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) such as a dyer or baker. According to the general rule (qiyas), a trustee is not liable for loss of entrusted property without negligence. However, by istihsan, the common hired worker is held liable for loss of goods in his possession, unless the loss is unavoidable (like a fire). The reason is to prevent him from over-accepting work beyond his capacity for profit, which would endanger people's property. This ruling is also adopted by the Maliki school as maslaha mursala. The second example involves the rule that one who pays another's debt without his order is a volunteer and cannot claim reimbursement. However, by istihsan, if the payer is compelled to pay (e.g., to release his own pledged property), he can reclaim the amount. This is considered istihsan because the general rule would lead to hardship for the payer. The author provides a reference to the detailed ruling in Durr al-Mukhtar and Radd al-Muhtar. These examples illustrate how istihsan operates to prevent hardship and serve public interest within the Hanafi legal framework.

Key Terms
الأجير الخاص (al-ajir al-khas): A private hired worker who sells all his time to a single hirer and does not work for others during that period.
الأجير المشترك (al-ajir al-mushtarak): A common hired worker who sells his work in a specific profession to all customers, e.g., dyer, baker, carpenter.
استحسان الضرورة (istihsan al-darurah): Juristic preference due to necessity; overriding a qiyas ruling to avoid hardship or serve public interest when the ʿillah of necessity is present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because he is more negligent than private workers
B) To prevent him from over-accepting work and endangering property
C) Because he earns more profit and can afford compensation
D) Because the customer has no other means of recourse

Key Takeaway
Istihsan al-darurah provides a principled exception to qiyas when strict analogy leads to hardship, as in the liability of common workers and the right of reimbursement for compulsory payments.

Istihsan Overriding Qiyas: Agency Set-Off and Bread Loans
Providing two case studies where istihsan overrides apparent qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of istihsan (by qiyas and of necessity) and apply the maxim 'istihsan takes precedence over qiyas' to new cases in mu'amalat.

Core Idea
Istihsan allows departing from strict analogy when necessity, custom, or a hidden analogy demands ease.

This passage dives into two concrete examples where the Hanafi school sets aside apparent qiyas in favor of istihsan. The first involves an agent who pays from his own pocket intending to recoup from the principal's deposit; strict qiyas would deem him a donor, but istihsan permits set-off to facilitate assistance. The second permits borrowing bread by count despite weight variation, because custom treats minor differences as negligible and the transaction is not for profit. These examples ground the maxim that istihsan overrides qiyas when they conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Qawida
State the maxim that governs both examples: 'Istihsan takes precedence over qiyas when they conflict.' Note its rank (sughra) and scope (mu'amalat).
The source directly states this conclusion at the end.
2
Analyze the First Furu' (Agent Case)
Work through the agency scenario: the agent pays from his own money intending to recoup. Under qiyas, he is a donor (mutabarri') and must return the deposit. Under istihsan, set-off (muqassa) is applied. Identify the stronger evidence: removing hardship and facilitating cooperation.
This is istihsan by qiyas (hidden analogy).
3
Analyze the Second Furu' (Bread Loan)
Borrowing bread by count among neighbors: qiyas prohibits due to riba al-fadl in weighable goods. Istihsan permits because weight variation is negligible by custom, and necessity and lack of profiteering override the strict analogy.
This is istihsan of necessity.
4
Distinguish the Two Types of Istihsan
Categorize each example: the agent case is istihsan by qiyas (a hidden analogy); the bread loan is istihsan of necessity (need and custom). Note that both override apparent qiyas.
The source explicitly mentions both types.
5
Apply the Istithna'
Identify when istihsan cannot override qiyas: where qiyas is based on a clear text (nass). Explain that istihsan only applies when qiyas is not definitive.
The qawida 'لا اجتهاد مع النص' governs this exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل (٤) المصادر التبعية الاستحسان

وعلى هذا إذا سلَّم أحد إلى غيره مالاً وأمره أن يشتري به شيئاً أو يقضي عنه به دينه، أو ينفق له منه على عياله أو بنائه ونحو ذلك، فأمسك المأمور عنده ما سُلم إليه، واشترى أو قضى أو أنفق من مال نفسه فيما أمره الدافع بقصد أن يستوفي بعد ذلك مما دفعه إليه، فمقتضى القياس الظاهر أن يعتبر المأمور متبرعاً بالدفع ويرد إلى الآمر ما أخذ منه. ولكن قالوا أنه في الاستحسان لا يعتبر متبرعاً تيسيراً للمعونات، ودفعاً للحرج في سبيلها، فيجري التقاص بين ما ماله دفع من وبين ما في يده من مال الآمر ( ر ) رد المحتار كتاب الوكالة ٤ / ٤١٥) .

٣ - إنَّ الأموال الكيلية أو الوزنية تعد شرعاً من الأموال الربوية التي يجري فيها ربا الفضل أي لا يجوز إقراض شيء منها واستيفاء أكثر منه . وكذا لا يجوز بيع بعضها بمقدار من جنسه أكثر منه . ولكن فقهاء الحنفية حكموا بجواز استقراض الخبز عدداً بين الجيران، وإن تفاوت وزن الأرغفة التفاوت المعتاد ؛ استحساناً على خلاف القياس، نظراً للضرورة وحاجة الناس مع انتفاء فكرة الربا والاسترباح في هذه العملية، لأنَّ هذا التفاوت من التوافه المهدرة عرفاً (۱). ر رد المحتار ١٧٢/٤ و ١٨٧.
(1) ينبغي أن يعتبر مثل ذلك في صرف النقود الفضية ونحوها بأجزائها الصغرى عندما يكون وزن مجموع الأجزاء أقل أو أكثر من وزن القطعة المستبدل بها. ويتردد اليوم بعضهم في ذلك غلواً وتشدداً محرجاً في الدين بلا موجب، مع أن هذا الصرف أشد حاجة وأولى بالجواز الشرعي من استقراض الخبز عدداً بين الجيران، لأن الأجزاء المستبدلة والقطعة النقدية المستبدل بها متساويان قيمة وعرفاً، ولا يصلح ذلك ذريعة للمراباة والاسترباح.

٤ - هذه أمثلة هي قليل من كثير من المسائل الاستحسانية المنبثة في الفقه الحنفي من كلا النوعين أعني الاستحسان القياسي واستحسان الضرورة. ومنها يتضح أنَّ الاستحسان مقدَّم على القياس عند تعارضهما.
Chapter 4: Subsidiary Sources – Istihsan. And upon this: If one gives money to another and orders him to buy something with it, or to pay his debt with it, or to spend on his family or building etc., then the agent withholds what was given to him, and buys, pays, or spends from his own money in what the principal ordered him, intending to then recover from what the principal had given him – then the apparent qiyas would deem the agent a donor and require him to return what he took from the principal. But they said that on istihsan he is not considered a donor, to facilitate acts of assistance and remove hardship from them. So set-off (muqassa) is applied between what he paid from his own money and what he holds of the principal's money. (Radd al-Muhtar, Kitab al-Wakala, 4/415). 3. Goods sold by measure or by weight are considered by law to be ribawi goods in which riba al-fadl applies, i.e., it is not permissible to lend any of them and receive more in return. Likewise, it is not permissible to sell some of them for a larger amount of the same type. But the Hanafi jurists ruled that borrowing bread by count among neighbors is permissible, even if there is the usual variation in the weight of the loaves, as istihsan contrary to qiyas, due to necessity and the need of people, combined with the absence of the idea of riba and profiteering in this transaction, because this variation is considered negligible (from the custom). (Radd al-Muhtar 4/172 & 187). (1) Such should be considered in the exchange of silver coins and the like with their small parts when the total weight of the parts is less or more than the weight of the piece being exchanged. Some people today hesitate on this, going to extremes and excessive strictness in religion without cause, even though this exchange is more needed and more deserving of permissibility by Shariah than borrowing bread by count among neighbors, because the exchanged parts and the coin piece are equal in value and custom, and this does not serve as a means for usury and profiteering. 4. These examples are few among many istihsani issues scattered in Hanafi fiqh from both types, namely istihsan by qiyas and istihsan of necessity. And from them it is clear that istihsan is given precedence over qiyas when they conflict.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a set of examples demonstrating istihsan (juristic preference) overriding qiyas (analogy) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by presenting two concrete cases. First, the case of an agent (wakeel) who, instead of using the principal's money as instructed, pays from his own pocket intending to later recoup from the principal's money held by him. According to strict qiyas, the agent is a donor (mutabarri') and must return what he took. But istihsan says he is not a donor, allowing set-off (muqassa) between his payment and the principal's deposit. This is based on ease and removal of hardship, facilitating cooperation. Second, the classical issue of borrowing loaves of bread by count among neighbors. Although bread is a weighable commodity (mawzoonat) and normally subject to riba al-fadl (usury of excess) – meaning you cannot lend one loaf and receive a heavier loaf back – the Hanafis permit this as istihsan. The rationale is that the slight weight differences are negligible in custom and the transaction is for mutual assistance, not profit. The author adds a modern application: exchanging silver coins for smaller denominations where total weight may differ; this should be allowed similarly because the value is equal and custom disregards small weight differences. The passage concludes that these are examples of both types of istihsan: istihsan by qiyas (where a hidden analogy overrides the apparent one) and istihsan of necessity (due to need). The key takeaway is that istihsan takes precedence over qiyas when they conflict.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (istihsan): A subsidiary source of law where a ruling is preferred over an apparent analogy due to a stronger indication (dalil) of necessity, custom, or hidden analogy.
القياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a common effective cause ('illa).
التقاص (muqassa): Set-off; cancelling mutual debts between two parties to the extent of the smaller amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Hanafi jurists permit borrowing bread by count among neighbors despite the general prohibition of riba al-fadl in weighable goods?
A) Because bread is not a ribawi commodity.
B) Because of necessity and the customary disregard for small weight differences.
C) Because the lender and borrower are relatives.
D) Because the bread is given as a gift, not a loan.

Key Takeaway
Istihsan is a legitimate Hanafi source that overrides qiyas when necessity, custom, or a hidden analogy demands ease.

Maliki Istihsan: Definition and Evidence
Defines Maliki istihsan and its justification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Maliki definition of istihsan, list its three triggers, and cite the Quranic and hadith evidence that justify it.

Core Idea
Maliki istihsan abandons apparent qiyas for custom, interest, or hardship.

This passage introduces the Maliki conception of istihsan, distinguishing it from the Hanafi usage. Unlike the Hanafis, who equate istihsan with hidden analogy, the Malikis define istihsan as setting aside an apparent analogy when it conflicts with a prevailing custom, a preponderant interest, or when it leads to hardship. The author supports this method with Quranic verses and the prophetic hadith 'no harm and no reciprocating harm,' establishing istihsan as a legitimate source of law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maliki definition of istihsan
Read the passage carefully to understand that Malikis do not call hidden analogy istihsan. Instead, they define it as abandoning apparent qiyas for one of three reasons.
2
List the three triggers
Extract the three reasons: 1) a prevailing custom ('urf ghalib), 2) a preponderant interest (maslaha rajiha), 3) hardship (haraj).
These triggers override the apparent qiyas.
3
Cite the textual evidence
The author cites Quran 2:185 (ease), 22:78 (no hardship), and the hadith 'no harm and no reciprocating harm' as proof that istihsan is grounded in sharia.
These texts mandate removal of hardship and observance of interest.
4
Understand the underlying principle
Recognize that istihsan is a means to achieve justice and avoid rigor, as Ibn Rushd stated: 'turning to interest and justice.'
This is similar to Hanafi istihsan of necessity.

الباب الثاني : مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
المصلحة التطبيقية
(1).
وقد أخذ الاجتهاد المالكي أيضاً بطريقة الاستحسان وتوسع فيها أكثر من الحنفية علاجاً لغلو القياس. ولكن المالكية لا يسمون القياس الخفي استحساناً كما في اصطلاح الحنفية، وإنما الاستحسان عند المالكية أن يترك القياس الظاهر لأحد أمور ثلاثة :
إذا عارضه عُرْف غالب، أي عادة شائعة.
أو عارضته مصلحة راجحة.
أو أدى إلى حرج ومشقة.
فيكون الحكم الاستحساني عندهم أيضاً من قبيل ترجيح مصلحة جزئية في حكم معين كانت تقضي القواعد القياسية بخلافه. وذلك لأن نصوص الشريعة الإسلامية تضافرت على وجوب رعاية المصلحة ودفع الحرج. كقوله تعالى : يُرِيدُ اللهُ بِكُمُ الْيُسْرَ وَلَا يُرِيدُ بِكُمُ الْمُسْرَ ) (سورة البقرة (١٨٥/٢) وقوله أيضاً : ﴿وَمَا جَعَلَ عَلَيْكُمْ فِي الدِّينِ مِنْ حَرَجٌ ) . (سورة الحج (۷۸/۲۲) وقول النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: (لا ضرر ولا ضرار» (۲) قال القاضي ابن رشد الحفيد المالكي في بداية المجتهد (١٥٤/٢) : ومعنى
الاستحسان في أكثر الأحوال هو الالتفات إلى المصلحة والعدل».
(۱) المأثور عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه كان يقيس حتى إذا قبح القياس وأدى إلى غلو في الحكم ،استحسن أي عدل عنه إلى الاستحسان.
(۲)
وقد قال تلميذه الإمام محمد بن الحسن الشيباني: كان أبو حنيفة إذا قاس نازعه أصحابه المقاييس، فإذا قال: استحسن، لم يلحق به أحد (ر: كتاب «أبو حنيفة» للأستاذ الشيخ محمد أبي زهرة القسم الثاني ف ۱۷۲ . وكتاب «مالك له أيضاً، القسم الثاني ف/ ۱۷۲).
،
الحديث الثاني والثلاثون من الأربعين النووية. وقال النووي: حديث حسن، رواه ابن ماجة والدارقطني وغيرهما مسنداً، ورواه مالك في الموطأ عن عمرو بن يحيى أبيه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مرسلاً، فأسقط أبا سعيد الخدري) وله طرقٌ يَقْوى بعضها ببعض انتهى (ر: ف ۱۷/۱)
عن
٩٦

الفصل (٤) المصادر التبعية الاستحسان
وهذا في الحقيقة نظير استحسان الضرورة في الاجتهاد الحنفي.
١٠/٤ - ومن
الأمثلة
التي يبرز فيها غلو اطراد القياس الظاهر
وجوره، واختلف الاجتهاد في معالجتها بالاستحسان القضية المعروفة باسم المسألة المشتركة في الفرائض أي في أحكام الميراث، وهي أن تموت امرأة عن زوج، وأم، وأخوين لأم، وأخوين شقيقين .
فالزوج والأم والإخوة لأم هم من أصحاب الفرائض الإرثية المحددة. أما الأخوة الأشقاء فهم من العَصَبات (۱) . والقاعدة في الميراث هي: أنَّ العصبات إنما يأخذون ما يزيد عن أصحاب الفرائض .
فمقتضى القواعد القياسية في هذه الحادثة هو: أن يرث الإخوة لأم ولا يرث الأشقاء، لأن الفريضة الإرثية للزوج هنا نصف التركة؛ وللأم السدس؛ وللإخوة من الأم الثلث، فلا يبقى شيء للإخوة الأشقاء وهم العصبات. وهذا يؤدي إلى مشكلة من الغرابة بمكان، إذ يرث عندئذ الأخ لأم، ويحرم الشقيق !! وإلى هذا ذهب بعض الصحابة، وعليه الاجتهادان الحنفي والحنبلي.
ولكن عمر بن الخطاب وفريقاً آخر
من الصحابة رضي
الله
عنهم ذهبوا
إلى اشتراك الأشقاء الإخوة لأم في نصيبهم بالثلث استحساناً، باعتبار أنَّ الجميع أولاد أم واحدة، فالأشقاء يشاركونهم في سبب الإرث من جهة
الأم.
وبذلك سنّ عمر سُنَّة الاستحسان المقيم للعدالة الدافع للحرج، وإلى
هذا ذهب الاجتهادان المالكي والشافعي، وهو الأوجه.
(۱) العصبة في اصطلاح علم الفرائض هو كل قريب ذكر يتصل إلى الميت بمحض الذكورة، أي لا يدخل في نسبته إلى الميت أنثى، وذلك كالعم وابنه، وكالأخ وابنه، فإنهم من العصبات بخلاف العمة مثلاً لأنها أنثى، وبخلاف الخال وابنه لأن واسطة قرابتهما الأم وهي أنثى .
Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Jurisprudence
Applied Interest (1).
Maliki jurisprudence also adopted the method of istihsan and expanded it more than the Hanafis as a treatment for the extremity of qiyas. But the Malikis do not call hidden analogy istihsan as in Hanafi terminology. Rather, istihsan according to the Malikis is to abandon apparent qiyas for one of three reasons:
- If a prevailing custom ('urf ghalib) opposes it, i.e., a common habit.
- Or a preponderant interest (maslaha rajiha) opposes it.
- Or it leads to hardship and difficulty.
Thus, the istihsani ruling according to them is also of the type of preferring a particular interest in a specific ruling whose analogical rules would dictate otherwise. This is because the texts of Islamic law have corroborated the necessity of observing interest and repelling hardship. Such as His statement: "Allah intends for you ease and does not intend for you hardship" (Surah al-Baqarah 2:185) and also His statement: "And He has not placed upon you in the religion any hardship" (Surah al-Hajj 22:78) and the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: "No harm and no reciprocating harm" (2). Judge Ibn Rushd the grandson, the Maliki, said in Bidayat al-Mujtahid (2/154): "The meaning of istihsan in most cases is turning to interest and justice."
(1) It is narrated from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, that he would analogize until when the analogy became ugly and led to extremeness in the ruling, he would practice istihsan, i.e., turn away to istihsan.
(2) His student Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani said: Abu Hanifa, when he would analogize, his companions would contest him with analogies. But when he said 'I practice istihsan', no one could catch up with him (see: book 'Abu Hanifa' by Prof. Sheikh Muhammad Abu Zahra, part two, p. 172; and his book 'Malik' also, part two, p. 172).
The thirty-second hadith of the Forty Nawawi. Al-Nawawi said: A good hadith, narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Daraqutni and others with a chain, and Malik narrated it in al-Muwatta' from 'Amr ibn Yahya from his father from the Prophet, peace be upon him, as a mursal, omitting Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, and it has paths that strengthen each other (see: p. 1/17).

Chapter (4) Subsidiary Sources: Istihsan
This is in reality similar to istihsan of necessity in Hanafi jurisprudence.
10/4 - Among the examples that highlight the extremeness and injustice of applying apparent qiyas consistently, and where ijtihad differed in treating it with istihsan, is the well-known issue called 'al-mas'ala al-mushtaraka' in fara'id, i.e., inheritance rulings. It is that a woman dies leaving a husband, a mother, two uterine brothers, and two full brothers.
The husband, mother, and uterine brothers are among the fixed-share heirs. As for the full brothers, they are 'asabat (1). The rule in inheritance is that the 'asabat only take what remains after the fixed-share heirs.
Thus, the requirement of analogical rules in this case is that the uterine brothers inherit and the full brothers do not inherit, because the fixed share of the husband here is half the estate, for the mother one-sixth, for the uterine brothers one-third, leaving nothing for the full brothers who are 'asabat. This leads to a strange problem: the uterine brother inherits while the full brother is deprived! This is the view of some Companions, and upon it are the Hanafi and Hanbali schools.
But 'Umar ibn al-Khattab and another group of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, held that the full brothers share with the uterine brothers in their one-third portion as an istihsan, considering that all are children of one mother, so the full brothers share with them in the cause of inheritance from the mother's side.
Thus 'Umar established a sunnah of istihsan that establishes justice and repels hardship. The Maliki and Shafi'i schools adopted this, and it is the stronger view.
(1) 'Asaba in the terminology of fara'id science is every male relative who is connected to the deceased through exclusively males, i.e., no female enters into his relation to the deceased, such as the paternal uncle and his son, and the brother and his son; they are among the 'asabat, unlike the paternal aunt because she is female, and unlike the maternal uncle and his son because the intermediate in their kinship is the mother, who is female.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage discusses the Maliki conception of istihsan and provides a concrete inheritance example. The author, Mustafa al-Zarqa, first clarifies that unlike the Hanafis, the Malikis do not call hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) istihsan. Instead, for them, istihsan is abandoning an apparent qiyas (qiyas jali) when it conflicts with a prevalent custom, a preponderant interest, or when it leads to hardship. This is justified by Quranic verses (2:185, 22:78) and the hadith 'no harm and no reciprocating harm.' The author cites Ibn Rushd, who equates istihsan with attending to interest and justice. The passage notes that this Maliki approach parallels the Hanafi 'istihsan of necessity.' The key example is the 'common case' in inheritance (al-mas'ala al-mushtaraka): a woman dies leaving a husband (1/2), mother (1/6), two uterine brothers (1/3), and two full brothers. Under strict qiyas, the uterine brothers take the whole 1/3, leaving nothing for the full brothers (who are 'asaba). This seems unjust because the full brothers share the same mother as the uterine brothers. The Hanafi and Hanbali schools follow this strict qiyas. However, 'Umar ibn al-Khattab and others (followed by Maliki and Shafi'i schools) made the full brothers share equally with the uterine brothers in the 1/3 as an istihsan, because all are children of the same mother. This is presented as the stronger view, as it realizes justice and removes hardship. The passage thus illustrates how istihsan overrides a problematic analogy.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (istihsan): Maliki: abandoning apparent qiyas for a stronger reason (custom, interest, or hardship). Hanafi: preferring a hidden analogy or exception based on a stronger evidence.
المصلحة (maslaha): A preponderant interest that justifies abandoning qiyas in istihsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Maliki definition of istihsan presented in the passage, which of the following is NOT a valid reason to abandon apparent qiyas?
A) When the qiyas contradicts a prevailing custom
B) When the qiyas conflicts with a preponderant interest
C) When the qiyas leads to hardship
D) When the qiyas is considered weak due to a hidden analogy

Key Takeaway
Maliki istihsan is a valid method of ijtihad that abandons apparent qiyas when it conflicts with custom, interest, or hardship, supported by Quranic and hadith evidence.
